i want a comprehensive set of visual resources, educational content, and user guides to enhance the TendProcure web application and ensure a seamless user experience.  that will leverage expertise in user experience design, content creation, and multimedia production to deliver the following: 
Visual Tutorials and Presentations:
- Tender Process Walkthrough (Video): An engaging, animated video that guides users through the end-to-end tender management lifecycle, covering each step from Notice Inviting Tender to Final Completion.
- Bid Submission Tutorials (Video): A series of short, step-by-step video tutorials demonstrating the various features and capabilities of the bid submission process, including document preparation, cost analysis, timeline planning, and team collaboration.
- Vendor Onboarding (Presentation): An interactive presentation that explains the vendor registration and prequalification process, highlighting the required information, documentation, and compliance checks.
- Contract Management Fundamentals (Video): A video tutorial that delves into the key aspects of contract management, such as understanding contract terms, tracking performance metrics, managing change orders, and navigating the renewal process.
- Property Maintenance and Service Management (Animation): An animated explainer that showcases the property management features, including maintenance schedules, service categories, compliance inspections, and performance monitoring.
Interactive Guides and Infographics:
- Tender Creation Wizard (Interactive Guide): A step-by-step, interactive guide that assists users in creating new tenders, with AI-powered suggestions, document attachments, and approval workflow configuration.
- Bid Submission Checklist (Infographic): A visually appealing infographic that outlines the key steps and requirements for submitting a successful bid, providing a quick reference for contractors and vendors.
- Vendor Evaluation Criteria (Infographic): An infographic that clearly explains the various factors and scoring mechanisms used in the vendor prequalification and evaluation process.
- Contract Lifecycle Management (Interactive Guide): An interactive guide that allows users to navigate through the different stages of the contract management process, highlighting key milestones and actionable steps.
- Property Maintenance Planning (Infographic): An infographic that provides a comprehensive overview of the property maintenance categories, schedules, and compliance requirements.
FAQ and Blog Content:
- TendProcure FAQ Section: A comprehensive FAQ section that addresses common questions and concerns from users, covering topics such as tender creation, bid submission, vendor registration, contract management, and platform features.
- TendProcure Blog: A regularly updated blog that provides educational and informative content, including:
  - Industry insights and market trends
  - Best practices for tender management and procurement
  - Case studies and success stories
  - Tips and strategies for vendors and contractors
  - Thought leadership articles on procurement excellence
  - Updates on new features and platform enhancements
By incorporating these visual resources, interactive guides, and educational content throughout the TendProcure web application, you will create a highly engaging and user-friendly experience for all site visitors. The combination of multimedia elements, step-by-step tutorials, and informative blog posts will not only enhance the overall aesthetics of the platform but also empower users with the knowledge and confidence to navigate the tender management and procurement processes effectively.
i want  to ensure the visual branding, tone, and messaging align with the TendProcure brand identity, providing a cohesive and professional experience for all users. Additionally, I continuously want update and expand the content library, ensuring the platform remains relevant and valuable target audience.

1. Interactive Guide Boilerplate
interactive-guides/tender-wizard.html
<!DOCTYPE html>
<html lang="en">
<head>
  <meta charset="UTF-8">
  <title>Tender Creation Wizard</title>
  <link rel="stylesheet" href="tender-wizard.css">
</head>
<body>
  <div id="wizard-container">
    <h1>Create New Tender</h1>
    <div id="steps"></div>
    <div id="controls">
      <button id="prev">Back</button>
      <button id="next">Next</button>
    </div>
  </div>
  <script src="tender-wizard.js"></script>
</body>
</html>
interactive-guides/tender-wizard.css
body { font-family: sans-serif; background: #f9fafb; color: #333; padding: 2rem; }
#wizard-container { max-width: 600px; margin: auto; background: white; padding: 1.5rem; border-radius: .5rem; box-shadow: 0 2px 8px rgba(0,0,0,0.1); }
#steps { margin: 1rem 0; }
button { padding: .5rem 1rem; border: none; border-radius: .25rem; cursor: pointer; }
interactive-guides/tender-wizard.js
const steps = [
  { title: 'Basic Info', render: () => `<p>Enter tender title, description...</p>` },
  { title: 'Attachments', render: () => `<p>Upload documents & AI suggestions...</p>` },
  { title: 'Workflow', render: () => `<p>Set approval stages & notifications...</p>` }
];
let current = 0;
const stepsEl = document.getElementById('steps');
function render() {
  stepsEl.innerHTML = `<h2>${steps[current].title}</h2>` + steps[current].render();
}
document.getElementById('next').onclick = () => { if (current < steps.length-1) current++; render(); };
document.getElementById('prev').onclick = () => { if (current > 0) current--; render(); };
render();
(Repeat similarly for contract-lifecycle interactive guide.)

2. FAQ Section (faq/tendprocure-faq.html)
<section id="faq">
  <h2>Frequently Asked Questions</h2>
  <dl>
    <dt>How do I create a tender?</dt>
    <dd>Go to Tender Management ‚Üí New Tender, fill in details, attach docs, then Submit.</dd>
    <!-- Add all Q&A pairs here -->
  </dl>
</section>
<style>
  #faq { max-width: 800px; margin: auto; padding: 2rem; }
  dt { font-weight: bold; margin-top: 1rem; }
  dd { margin-left: 1rem; }
</style>
3. Blog Template (blog/blog-template.html)
<html><head><title>TendProcure Blog</title>
<link rel="stylesheet" href="blog.css"></head><body>
  <header><h1>TendProcure Insights</h1></header>
  <main id="posts"></main>
  <script>
    const posts = [
      { title: 'Industry Trends', date: '2025-06-01', excerpt: 'Explore the latest in procurement...', link: '#' },
      // more sample posts
    ];
    const container = document.getElementById('posts');
    posts.forEach(p => {
      container.innerHTML += `<article><h2>${p.title}</h2><p>${p.excerpt}</p><a href='${p.link}'>Read more</a></article>`;
    });
  </script>
</body></html>

from pptx import Presentation

# Create a new presentation
prs = Presentation()

# Slide titles for a 16-slide Vendor Onboarding deck
titles = [
    "Vendor Onboarding Overview",
    "Why Register with TendProcure?",
    "Step 1: Account Registration",
    "Step 2: Company Information",
    "Step 3: Documentation Requirements",
    "Step 4: Compliance & Verification",
    "Step 5: Prequalification Criteria",
    "Step 6: Scoring & Evaluation",
    "Step 7: Contract Terms Overview",
    "Step 8: Platform Navigation",
    "Step 9: Bid Submission Basics",
    "Step 10: Support & Resources",
    "Best Practices & Tips",
    "Security & Data Privacy",
    "Next Steps & Timeline",
    "Thank You & Contact Info"
]

# Choose layout indices: 0 = Title Slide, 1 = Title and Content
for i, title in enumerate(titles):
    layout = prs.slide_layouts[0] if i == 0 else prs.slide_layouts[1]
    slide = prs.slides.add_slide(layout)
    slide.shapes.title.text = title
    if layout == prs.slide_layouts[1]:
        body = slide.shapes.placeholders[1].text_frame
        body.text = "‚Ä¢ [Add your content here]"
        # Add additional placeholder bullets
        for _ in range(2):
            p = body.add_paragraph()
            p.text = "‚Ä¢ [Detail ...]"
            p.level = 1

# Save to file
output_path = "/mnt/data/vendor-onboarding.pptx"
prs.save(output_path)

output_path

Prompt Title:
TendProcure ‚Äì Complete Visual Asset Suite for a Modern Tender & Procurement Web App

Prompt Body:

Create a professional, branded suite of videos and animated explainers for a web-based tender and property procurement management platform called TendProcure. Visual tone should be clean, modern, and minimalistic, using glassmorphism, cool tones (navy, slate, cyan), and futuristic icons and UI wireframe effects.

Use smooth transitions, bold captions, clear animated text, and optional voiceovers (neutral professional tone, UK or US accent) to explain each step. Here are the videos I want created:

üé• 1. Tender Process Walkthrough (3 mins)

Notice Inviting Tender (NIT)

Document Upload

Bid Evaluation

Vendor Selection

Contract Signing

Final Completion & Reporting

Visual Style: Animated workflow diagrams, contract folders, digital signatures, milestones lighting up, dashboards updating in real-time.

üé• 2. Bid Submission Tutorial Series (5 videos √ó 2‚Äì3 mins)
Break down each video as a micro-lesson:

Preparing Tender Documents ‚Äì Formats, required fields, and templates.

Cost Analysis & Budgeting ‚Äì Excel upload, cost preview animations.

Timeline Planning ‚Äì Gantt chart or timeline animation.

Collaborating with Your Team ‚Äì User roles, task assignment.

Submitting a Bid ‚Äì Final checks, status animations.

Use UI walkthroughs (mock dashboard clicks) and overlayed guides for each video.

üé• 3. Vendor Onboarding Presentation (Convert to video)
16-step explainer of vendor registration and compliance, converted from a PowerPoint (use slide transitions, voiceover, and callouts).

Include visuals of company logos, IDs, compliance stamps, uploaded licenses, and evaluation scores.

üé• 4. Contract Management Fundamentals (4 mins)
Cover contract setup, milestone tracking, document amendments, renewal workflows.

Show visual charts updating, status badges, and performance KPI monitoring.

üé• 5. Property Maintenance & Service Management (2 mins)
Animated scenes of scheduling repairs, service types (plumbing, janitorial, landscaping), inspection workflows.

Include performance dashboards and compliance inspection logs.

Global Branding Instructions:

Logo (if available) appears in corner or intro.

Caption font: Open Sans or Roboto.

Background music: Light, tech-corporate style.

Use branded color palette (navy #1B2E4B, cyan #2DD4BF, slate #64748B).

from fpdf import FPDF

# Create PDF document with the Pictory/FlexClip prompt
pdf = FPDF()
pdf.add_page()
pdf.set_auto_page_break(auto=True, margin=15)

# Set fonts
pdf.set_font("Arial", size=12)
title = "TendProcure ‚Äì Master Visual Asset Suite Prompt"
pdf.set_font("Arial", 'B', 16)
pdf.multi_cell(0, 10, title)
pdf.ln()

# Reset font for content
pdf.set_font("Arial", size=12)

# Text content (shortened per page limit, full content is long)
prompt_text = """
Create a professional, branded suite of videos and animated explainers for a web-based tender and property procurement management platform called TendProcure. Use glassmorphism UI, clean transitions, cool tones (navy, cyan), and futuristic wireframes.

VIDEOS TO GENERATE:

1. Tender Process Walkthrough (3 mins):
Walkthrough full tender lifecycle: NIT ‚Üí Evaluation ‚Üí Contract Signing. Show dashboards, workflows, digital signatures.

2. Bid Submission Series (5 x 2‚Äì3 mins):
- Preparing Documents
- Cost & Budget Planning
- Timeline Planning
- Team Collaboration
- Submitting the Bid

3. Vendor Onboarding (Presentation ‚Üí Video):
Animate 16-slide onboarding steps. Show compliance upload, company info, scoring.

4. Contract Management (4 mins):
Contract setup, KPIs, renewal. Show charts, progress bars, notifications.

5. Property Management (2 mins):
Maintenance schedules, inspection logs, service categories.

GLOBAL INSTRUCTIONS:
- Use branding: navy #1B2E4B, cyan #2DD4BF, slate #64748B
- Include soft music, captions, CTA buttons, and branded outro
- Format: MP4, 1080p, named like 'bid-submission-01.mp4'

TAGLINE: ‚ÄúTendProcure ‚Äî Simplify. Submit. Succeed.‚Äù
"""

pdf.multi_cell(0, 10, prompt_text)

# Save PDF
output_pdf_path = "/mnt/data/TendProcure_VisualPrompt.pdf"
pdf.output(output_pdf_path)

# Last resort: Force all characters to ASCII using encoding workaround
import unicodedata

# Normalize and encode to ASCII
ascii_prompt_text = unicodedata.normalize('NFKD', prompt_text).encode('ascii', 'ignore').decode('ascii')

# Recreate PDF using ASCII-safe content
pdf = FPDF()
pdf.add_page()
pdf.set_auto_page_break(auto=True, margin=15)

pdf.set_font("Arial", 'B', 16)
pdf.multi_cell(0, 10, title)
pdf.ln()

pdf.set_font("Arial", size=12)
pdf.multi_cell(0, 10, ascii_prompt_text)

# Save the cleaned version
ascii_pdf_path = "/mnt/data/TendProcure_VisualPrompt.pdf"
pdf.output(ascii_pdf_path)

from reportlab.lib.pagesizes import letter
from reportlab.pdfgen import canvas

# Define output path
unicode_pdf_path = "/mnt/data/TendProcure_VisualPrompt.pdf"

# Create canvas with Unicode support
c = canvas.Canvas(unicode_pdf_path, pagesize=letter)
width, height = letter

# Title
c.setFont("Helvetica-Bold", 16)
c.drawString(50, height - 50, "TendProcure ‚Äì Master Visual Asset Suite Prompt")

# Body text
c.setFont("Helvetica", 10)

# Split content into lines manually for layout
lines = cleaned_prompt_text.split("\n")
y = height - 80
for line in lines:
    if y < 40:
        c.showPage()
        y = height - 40
        c.setFont("Helvetica", 10)
    c.drawString(50, y, line.strip())
    y -= 15

c.save()

Ultra, this script is solid‚Äîit flows like a guided user journey, packed with clear scenes and use-case highlights. But to really make it production-ready for video tools like Pictory, FlexClip, or Synthesia, I‚Äôd recommend breaking it into structured sections or ‚Äúscenes‚Äù, so the platform can assign animations, captions, voiceovers, or visuals per segment.

Here‚Äôs why:

Each line = 1 scene = 1 visual moment (much easier for editing and AI narration).

Tools like Pictory auto-split paragraphs, so pre-breaking helps pacing.

It also gives you room to insert B-roll, transitions, and overlays per topic.

    pdf.set_font("Arial", size=12)
    for line in lines:
        pdf.multi_cell(0, 10, f"- {line}")

import os
from zipfile import ZipFile

# Define paths
notion_markdown_path = "/mnt/data/TendProcure_Script.md"
zip_path = "/mnt/data/TendProcure_Assets.zip"

# Markdown content based on the scene-by-scene structure
markdown_content = "# TendProcure ‚Äì Full Visual Asset Script\n\n"

for title, lines in storyboard_scenes:
    markdown_content += f"## {title}\n"
    for line in lines:
        markdown_content += f"- {line}\n"
    markdown_content += "\n"

# Save markdown file
with open(notion_markdown_path, "w") as f:
    f.write(markdown_content)

# Create a zip archive
with ZipFile(zip_path, "w") as zipf:
    zipf.write(notion_markdown_path, arcname="TendProcure_Script.md")

from zipfile import ZipFile
from pathlib import Path

# Define file contents
dashboard_code = """
// üìä TendProcure Dashboard Component (Admin Overview)
// Requires: React, Recharts, Supabase Client

import React, { useEffect, useState } from 'react';
import { BarChart, Bar, XAxis, YAxis, Tooltip, ResponsiveContainer } from 'recharts';
import { supabase } from '../utils/supabaseClient';

const TenderStatsCard = () => {
  const [data, setData] = useState([]);

  useEffect(() => {
    fetchStats();
  }, []);

  const fetchStats = async () => {
    const { data: tenders, error } = await supabase
      .from('tenders')
      .select('status, count:status', { count: 'exact' })
      .group('status');

    if (!error) setData(tenders);
  };

  return (
    <div className="dashboard-card">
      <h2>Live Tender Count</h2>
      <ResponsiveContainer width="100%" height={300}>
        <BarChart data={data}>
          <XAxis dataKey="status" />
          <YAxis />
          <Tooltip />
          <Bar dataKey="count" fill="#0EA5E9" radius={[4, 4, 0, 0]} />
        </BarChart>
      </ResponsiveContainer>
    </div>
  );
};

export default TenderStatsCard;
"""

supabase_policy = """
-- Vendors see only their data
CREATE POLICY "Vendors can only see their data"
  ON "bids"
  FOR SELECT
  USING (vendor_id = auth.uid());

-- Optional: More secure write policies
CREATE POLICY "Vendors can only insert their bids"
  ON "bids"
  FOR INSERT
  WITH CHECK (vendor_id = auth.uid());
"""

mock_data = """
[
  { "status": "open", "count": 8 },
  { "status": "closed", "count": 4 },
  { "status": "draft", "count": 2 }
]
"""

export_script = """
import jsPDF from 'jspdf';

const generatePDF = () => {
  const doc = new jsPDF();
  doc.text("TendProcure Report - June", 20, 20);
  doc.text("Total Tenders: 14", 20, 40);
  doc.save("tender_report.pdf");
};
"""

readme = """
# TendProcure Dashboard Bundle

This package includes all components and helper tools for the TendProcure Admin Dashboard:

1. `TenderStatsCard.jsx`: React + Recharts component for real-time KPI chart.
2. `supabase_policies.sql`: Secure Supabase RLS policies.
3. `mock_data.json`: Dummy data for testing the frontend chart.
4. `export_pdf.js`: PDF export sample using jsPDF.

## Integration

- Add the `TenderStatsCard` to your Admin dashboard layout.
- Configure Supabase with the included policies for secure access.
- Use `mock_data.json` for testing before connecting to live DB.
- Call `generatePDF()` for exporting dashboard insights.
"""

# Define file paths
zip_path = "/mnt/data/TendProcure_Dashboard_Kit.zip"
file_structure = {
    "TenderStatsCard.jsx": dashboard_code,
    "supabase_policies.sql": supabase_policy,
    "mock_data.json": mock_data,
    "export_pdf.js": export_script,
    "README.txt": readme
}

# Create ZIP file
with ZipFile(zip_path, 'w') as zipf:
    for filename, content in file_structure.items():
        path = Path(f"/tmp/{filename}")
        path.write_text(content)
        zipf.write(path, arcname=filename)

zip_path

from zipfile import ZipFile
from pathlib import Path

# Recreate file contents after reset
dashboard_code = """
// üìä TendProcure Dashboard Component (Admin Overview)
// Requires: React, Recharts, Supabase Client

import React, { useEffect, useState } from 'react';
import { BarChart, Bar, XAxis, YAxis, Tooltip, ResponsiveContainer } from 'recharts';
import { supabase } from '../utils/supabaseClient';

const TenderStatsCard = () => {
  const [data, setData] = useState([]);

  useEffect(() => {
    fetchStats();
  }, []);

  const fetchStats = async () => {
    const { data: tenders, error } = await supabase
      .from('tenders')
      .select('status, count:status', { count: 'exact' })
      .group('status');

    if (!error) setData(tenders);
  };

  return (
    <div className="dashboard-card">
      <h2>Live Tender Count</h2>
      <ResponsiveContainer width="100%" height={300}>
        <BarChart data={data}>
          <XAxis dataKey="status" />
          <YAxis />
          <Tooltip />
          <Bar dataKey="count" fill="#0EA5E9" radius={[4, 4, 0, 0]} />
        </BarChart>
      </ResponsiveContainer>
    </div>
  );
};

export default TenderStatsCard;
"""

supabase_policy = """
-- Vendors see only their data
CREATE POLICY "Vendors can only see their data"
  ON "bids"
  FOR SELECT
  USING (vendor_id = auth.uid());

-- Optional: More secure write policies
CREATE POLICY "Vendors can only insert their bids"
  ON "bids"
  FOR INSERT
  WITH CHECK (vendor_id = auth.uid());
"""

mock_data = """
[
  { "status": "open", "count": 8 },
  { "status": "closed", "count": 4 },
  { "status": "draft", "count": 2 }
]
"""

export_script = """
import jsPDF from 'jspdf';

const generatePDF = () => {
  const doc = new jsPDF();
  doc.text("TendProcure Report - June", 20, 20);
  doc.text("Total Tenders: 14", 20, 40);
  doc.save("tender_report.pdf");
};
"""

readme = """

This package includes all components and helper tools for the TendProcure Admin Dashboard:

1. `TenderStatsCard.jsx`: React + Recharts component for real-time KPI chart.
2. `supabase_policies.sql`: Secure Supabase RLS policies.
3. `mock_data.json`: Dummy data for testing the frontend chart.
4. `export_pdf.js`: PDF export sample using jsPDF.

## Integration

- Add the `TenderStatsCard` to your Admin dashboard layout.
- Configure Supabase with the included policies for secure access.
- Use `mock_data.json` for testing before connecting to live DB.
- Call `generatePDF()` for exporting dashboard insights.
"""

# Define file paths

from zipfile import ZipFile
from pathlib import Path

# Define file contents for Contract Health Dashboard Components
contract_pie_chart = """
// üìä PieChart: Active vs Expired Contracts
import React, { useEffect, useState } from 'react';
import { PieChart, Pie, Cell, Tooltip, ResponsiveContainer } from 'recharts';
import { supabase } from '../utils/supabaseClient';

const COLORS = ['#10B981', '#EF4444', '#F59E0B'];

const ContractStatusPie = () => {
  const [data, setData] = useState([]);

  useEffect(() => {
    fetchData();
  }, []);

  const fetchData = async () => {
    const { data: contracts } = await supabase.from('contracts').select('status');
    const summary = contracts.reduce((acc, contract) => {
      acc[contract.status] = (acc[contract.status] || 0) + 1;
      return acc;
    }, {});
    const result = Object.entries(summary).map(([name, value]) => ({ name, value }));
    setData(result);
  };

  return (
    <ResponsiveContainer width="100%" height={250}>
      <PieChart>
        <Pie data={data} dataKey="value" nameKey="name" cx="50%" cy="50%" outerRadius={80}>
          {data.map((entry, index) => <Cell key={`cell-${index}`} fill={COLORS[index % COLORS.length]} />)}
        </Pie>
        <Tooltip />
      </PieChart>
    </ResponsiveContainer>
  );
};

export default ContractStatusPie;
"""

sla_breach_chart = """
// üìâ BarChart: SLA Breach Count by Month
import React, { useEffect, useState } from 'react';
import { BarChart, Bar, XAxis, YAxis, Tooltip, ResponsiveContainer } from 'recharts';
import { supabase } from '../utils/supabaseClient';

const SLABreachBarChart = () => {
  const [data, setData] = useState([]);

  useEffect(() => {
    fetchData();
  }, []);

  const fetchData = async () => {
    const { data: logs } = await supabase.from('inspections').select('sla_status, inspection_date');
    const monthly = logs.reduce((acc, log) => {
      const date = new Date(log.inspection_date);
      const month = `${date.getFullYear()}-${date.getMonth() + 1}`;
      if (log.sla_status === 'breach') {
        acc[month] = (acc[month] || 0) + 1;
      }
      return acc;
    }, {});
    const result = Object.entries(monthly).map(([month, breaches]) => ({ month, breaches }));
    setData(result);
  };

  return (
    <ResponsiveContainer width="100%" height={250}>
      <BarChart data={data}>
        <XAxis dataKey="month" />
        <YAxis />
        <Tooltip />
        <Bar dataKey="breaches" fill="#EF4444" />
      </BarChart>
    </ResponsiveContainer>
  );
};

export default SLABreachBarChart;
"""

readme = """
# Contract Health Dashboard Components

This bundle contains two key visual modules for the TendProcure contract dashboard:

1. `ContractStatusPie.jsx` ‚Äì PieChart showing status breakdown of contracts
2. `SLABreachBarChart.jsx` ‚Äì BarChart showing monthly SLA breaches

Usage:
- Import and include these components in the admin dashboard view.
- Ensure your Supabase tables `contracts` and `inspections` include fields:
  - contracts.status
  - inspections.sla_status and inspection_date

Each chart automatically processes and displays real-time data.
"""

# Define zip path and file structure
zip_path = "/mnt/data/TendProcure_Contract_Health_Charts.zip"
file_structure = {
    "ContractStatusPie.jsx": contract_pie_chart,
    "SLABreachBarChart.jsx": sla_breach_chart,
    "README.txt": readme
}

# Create zip archive
with ZipFile(zip_path, 'w') as zipf:
    for filename, content in file_structure.items():
        path = Path(f"/tmp/{filename}")
        path.write_text(content)
        zipf.write(path, arcname=filename)

from zipfile import ZipFile
from pathlib import Path

# Define content for AI Assistant Chat Flow components

assistant_prompt_framework = """
// üì¨ Prompt Framework: GPT-based Assistant Logic
const buildPrompt = ({ role, query, userId }) => {
  let context = "";

  if (role === "admin") {
    context = \`You are an intelligent assistant helping an admin manage tenders, vendors, and contracts. The user ID is \${userId}. Provide actionable insights from the Supabase data.\`;
  } else if (role === "vendor") {
    context = \`You are assisting a vendor with bidding status, contract issues, and deadlines. Limit insights to the vendor ID: \${userId}. Do not expose other data.\`;
  }

  return \`\${context}\\n\\nUser Query: \${query}\\nResponse:\`;
};

export default buildPrompt;
"""

data_resolver_function = """
// üß† Supabase Data Resolver for Assistant
// Receives natural language query -> fetches relevant Supabase data
import { supabase } from '../utils/supabaseClient';

export const resolveDataForQuery = async (query, userId, role) => {
  if (query.includes('my bids')) {
    const { data } = await supabase.from('bids').select('*').eq('vendor_id', userId);
    return { result: data };
  }
  if (query.includes('contracts expiring')) {
    const today = new Date().toISOString();
    const { data } = await supabase.from('contracts')
      .select('*')
      .lt('end_date', today)
      .eq(role === 'vendor' ? 'vendor_id' : 'admin_id', userId);
    return { result: data };
  }
  return { result: 'I couldn‚Äôt find anything for that query yet.' };
};
"""

chat_ui_snippet = """
// üí¨ Simple Chat UI (React)
import React, { useState } from 'react';
import buildPrompt from './buildPrompt';
import { resolveDataForQuery } from './dataResolver';

const AssistantChat = ({ user }) => {
  const [query, setQuery] = useState('');
  const [response, setResponse] = useState('');

  const handleSubmit = async () => {
    const prompt = buildPrompt({ role: user.role, query, userId: user.id });
    const { result } = await resolveDataForQuery(query, user.id, user.role);
    setResponse(JSON.stringify(result, null, 2));
  };

  return (
    <div className="chat-ui">
      <textarea value={query} onChange={e => setQuery(e.target.value)} placeholder="Ask something..." />
      <button onClick={handleSubmit}>Ask Assistant</button>
      <pre>{response}</pre>
    </div>
  );
};

export default AssistantChat;
"""

readme_content = """
# ü§ñ TendProcure AI Assistant Framework

This bundle includes:
1. `buildPrompt.js` - Context-aware assistant prompt builder (scoped by role)
2. `dataResolver.js` - Supabase query router for resolving user intents
3. `AssistantChat.jsx` - Basic React Chat UI for assistant module

## üõ† Integration Instructions

- Plug `AssistantChat` into any dashboard view (Admin or Vendor)
- Provide `user` prop with `{ id, role }`
- Customize `resolveDataForQuery` for more query types

## üß† GPT Integration
To connect to OpenAI:
- Send `buildPrompt()` to a GPT-4o completion endpoint with context
- Combine GPT response + Supabase data in final reply
"""

# File structure for zip
zip_path = "/mnt/data/TendProcure_AIAssistant_Kit.zip"
file_structure = {
    "buildPrompt.js": assistant_prompt_framework,
    "dataResolver.js": data_resolver_function,
    "AssistantChat.jsx": chat_ui_snippet,
    "README.txt": readme_content
}

# Create zip archive
with ZipFile(zip_path, 'w') as zipf:
    for filename, content in file_structure.items():
        path = Path(f"/tmp/{filename}")
        path.write_text(content)
        zipf.write(path, arcname=filename)

const buildPrompt = ({ role, query, userId }) => {
  let context = "";

  if (role === "admin") {
    context = `You are an intelligent assistant helping an admin manage tenders, vendors, and contracts. The user ID is ${userId}. Provide actionable insights from the Supabase data.`;
  } else if (role === "vendor") {
    context = `You are assisting a vendor with bidding status, contract issues, and deadlines. Limit insights to the vendor ID: ${userId}. Do not expose other data.`;
  }

  return `${context}\n\nUser Query: ${query}\nResponse:`;
};

export default buildPrompt;

import React, { useState } from 'react';
import buildPrompt from './buildPrompt';
import { resolveDataForQuery } from './dataResolver';

const AssistantChat = ({ user }) => {
  const [query, setQuery] = useState('');
  const [response, setResponse] = useState('');

  const handleSubmit = async () => {
    const prompt = buildPrompt({ role: user.role, query, userId: user.id });
    const { result } = await resolveDataForQuery(query, user.id, user.role);
    setResponse(JSON.stringify(result, null, 2));
  };

  return (
    <div className="chat-ui">
      <textarea value={query} onChange={e => setQuery(e.target.value)} placeholder="Ask something..." />
      <button onClick={handleSubmit}>Ask Assistant</button>
      <pre>{response}</pre>
    </div>
  );
};

export default AssistantChat;

from zipfile import ZipFile
from pathlib import Path

# Modern & expanded criteria for vendor scoring
vendor_scoring_logic = """
// üßÆ AI-Weighted Vendor Scoring Engine

const normalize = (val, min, max) => (val - min) / (max - min || 1);

export const calculateVendorScore = (vendor) => {
  const weights = {
    bidAccuracy: 0.12,
    onTimeDelivery: 0.15,
    maintenanceCompliance: 0.10,
    costCompetitiveness: 0.13,
    docCompleteness: 0.10,
    teamAvailability: 0.10,
    avgRating: 0.10,
    communicationResponsiveness: 0.10,
    innovation: 0.05,
    safetyIncidents: -0.05,
  };

  const normalized = {
    bidAccuracy: normalize(vendor.bidAccuracy, 0, 1),
    onTimeDelivery: normalize(vendor.onTimeDelivery, 0, 1),
    maintenanceCompliance: normalize(vendor.maintenanceCompliance, 0, 1),
    costCompetitiveness: normalize(1 - vendor.costDeviation, 0, 1),
    docCompleteness: normalize(vendor.docCompleteness, 0, 1),
    teamAvailability: normalize(vendor.teamAvailability, 0, 1),
    avgRating: normalize(vendor.avgRating, 0, 5),
    communicationResponsiveness: normalize(vendor.responseRate, 0, 1),
    innovation: normalize(vendor.innovationScore, 0, 1),
    safetyIncidents: normalize(vendor.safetyIncidents, 0, 5), // negative scoring
  };

  const score = Object.entries(weights).reduce((acc, [key, weight]) => {
    return acc + (normalized[key] * weight);
  }, 0);

  return Math.max(0, Math.min(100, score * 100)); // scale to 0‚Äì100
};
"""

vendor_score_table = """
// üìä React Table: Vendor Score Overview
import React from 'react';
import { calculateVendorScore } from './scoreVendors';

const VendorScoreTable = ({ vendors }) => {
  const rows = vendors.map(v => ({
    ...v,
    score: calculateVendorScore(v).toFixed(1),
  })).sort((a, b) => b.score - a.score);

  return (
    <table className="vendor-score-table">
      <thead>
        <tr>
          <th>Vendor</th>
          <th>Bid Accuracy</th>
          <th>Delivery</th>
          <th>Docs</th>
          <th>Rating</th>
          <th>Safety</th>
          <th>Score</th>
        </tr>
      </thead>
      <tbody>
        {rows.map((v, i) => (
          <tr key={i}>
            <td>{v.name}</td>
            <td>{v.bidAccuracy}</td>
            <td>{v.onTimeDelivery}</td>
            <td>{v.docCompleteness}</td>
            <td>{v.avgRating}</td>
            <td>{v.safetyIncidents}</td>
            <td><strong>{v.score}</strong></td>
          </tr>
        ))}
      </tbody>
    </table>
  );
};

export default VendorScoreTable;
"""

supabase_query_snippet = """
-- üîÑ Supabase Query to Collect Vendor Evaluation Metrics
SELECT
  v.id,
  v.name,
  v.doc_completeness,
  v.team_availability,
  v.response_rate,
  v.innovation_score,
  v.safety_incidents,
  AVG(b.is_accurate)::float AS bidAccuracy,
  AVG(c.on_time)::float AS onTimeDelivery,
  AVG(m.compliance_score)::float AS maintenanceCompliance,
  AVG(r.rating)::float AS avgRating,
  ABS(AVG(b.bid_price - t.avg_price)) / NULLIF(t.avg_price, 0)::float AS costDeviation
FROM vendors v
LEFT JOIN bids b ON b.vendor_id = v.id
LEFT JOIN contracts c ON c.vendor_id = v.id
LEFT JOIN maintenance_logs m ON m.vendor_id = v.id
LEFT JOIN vendor_reviews r ON r.vendor_id = v.id
LEFT JOIN (
  SELECT tender_id, AVG(bid_price) AS avg_price FROM bids GROUP BY tender_id
) t ON b.tender_id = t.tender_id
GROUP BY v.id, t.avg_price;
"""

readme = """
# üß† AI Vendor Scoring & Evaluation System

## Included
1. `scoreVendors.js` ‚Äì Smart scoring logic with customizable weights
2. `VendorScoreTable.jsx` ‚Äì React component to display ranked scores
3. `vendor_metrics.sql` ‚Äì Supabase query to fetch evaluation fields

## Instructions
- Use `scoreVendors.js` in your backend or client logic.
- Feed vendor data into `VendorScoreTable.jsx` for sorted display.
- Extend or tweak scoring weights and metrics as needed.
"""

# Prepare ZIP package
zip_path = "/mnt/data/TendProcure_VendorScoring_Kit.zip"
file_structure = {
    "scoreVendors.js": vendor_scoring_logic,
    "VendorScoreTable.jsx": vendor_score_table,
    "vendor_metrics.sql": supabase_query_snippet,
    "README.txt": readme

        path = Path(f"/tmp/{filename}")
        path.write_text(content)
        zipf.write(path, arcname=filename)

const normalize = (val, min, max) => (val - min) / (max - min || 1);

export const calculateVendorScore = (vendor) => {
  const weights = {
    bidAccuracy: 0.12,
    onTimeDelivery: 0.15,
    maintenanceCompliance: 0.10,
    costCompetitiveness: 0.13,
    docCompleteness: 0.10,
    teamAvailability: 0.10,
    avgRating: 0.10,
    communicationResponsiveness: 0.10,
    innovation: 0.05,
    safetyIncidents: -0.05,
  };

  const normalized = {
    bidAccuracy: normalize(vendor.bidAccuracy, 0, 1),
    onTimeDelivery: normalize(vendor.onTimeDelivery, 0, 1),
    maintenanceCompliance: normalize(vendor.maintenanceCompliance, 0, 1),
    costCompetitiveness: normalize(1 - vendor.costDeviation, 0, 1),
    docCompleteness: normalize(vendor.docCompleteness, 0, 1),
    teamAvailability: normalize(vendor.teamAvailability, 0, 1),
    avgRating: normalize(vendor.avgRating, 0, 5),
    communicationResponsiveness: normalize(vendor.responseRate, 0, 1),
    innovation: normalize(vendor.innovationScore, 0, 1),
    safetyIncidents: normalize(vendor.safetyIncidents, 0, 5),
  };

  const score = Object.entries(weights).reduce((acc, [key, weight]) => acc + (normalized[key] * weight), 0);
  return Math.max(0, Math.min(100, score * 100)); // scale to 0‚Äì100
};

import React from 'react';

const VendorScoreTable = ({ vendors }) => {
  const rows = vendors.map(v => ({
    ...v,
    score: calculateVendorScore(v).toFixed(1),
  })).sort((a, b) => b.score - a.score);

  return (
    <table>
      <thead>
        <tr>
          <th>Vendor</th>
          <th>Accuracy</th>
          <th>Delivery</th>
          <th>Docs</th>
          <th>Rating</th>
          <th>Safety</th>
          <th>Score</th>
        </tr>
      </thead>
      <tbody>
        {rows.map((v, i) => (
          <tr key={i}>
            <td>{v.name}</td>
            <td>{v.bidAccuracy}</td>
            <td>{v.onTimeDelivery}</td>
            <td>{v.docCompleteness}</td>
            <td>{v.avgRating}</td>
            <td>{v.safetyIncidents}</td>
            <td><strong>{v.score}</strong></td>
          </tr>
        ))}
      </tbody>
    </table>
  );
};

export default VendorScoreTable;
üîÑ vendor_metrics.sql
sql
Copy
Edit
SELECT
  v.id, v.name, v.doc_completeness, v.team_availability,
  v.response_rate, v.innovation_score, v.safety_incidents,
  AVG(b.is_accurate)::float AS bidAccuracy,
  AVG(c.on_time)::float AS onTimeDelivery,
  AVG(m.compliance_score)::float AS maintenanceCompliance,
  AVG(r.rating)::float AS avgRating,
  ABS(AVG(b.bid_price - t.avg_price)) / NULLIF(t.avg_price, 0)::float AS costDeviation
FROM vendors v
LEFT JOIN bids b ON b.vendor_id = v.id
LEFT JOIN contracts c ON c.vendor_id = v.id
LEFT JOIN maintenance_logs m ON m.vendor_id = v.id
LEFT JOIN vendor_reviews r ON r.vendor_id = v.id
LEFT JOIN (
  SELECT tender_id, AVG(bid_price) AS avg_price FROM bids GROUP BY tender_id
) t ON b.tender_id = t.tender_id
GROUP BY v.id, t.avg_price;

üìê Supabase Table Schema:
sql
Copy
Edit
CREATE TABLE feedback_submissions (
  id UUID PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT gen_random_uuid(),
  user_id UUID REFERENCES users(id),
  vendor_id UUID REFERENCES vendors(id),
  project_id UUID,
  satisfaction INT,
  clarity INT,
  communication INT,
  delivery INT,
  recommend BOOLEAN,
  comments TEXT,
  created_at TIMESTAMP DEFAULT now()
);
üß† Predictive Analytics: Risk & Performance Forecasting
üß© Module 2: Predictive Risk Insights
üéØ Key Forecast Metrics:
Metric	Source	Forecast Insight
üî¥ SLA Risk Score	SLA history + current tasks	Predict if SLA will be breached
üìâ Vendor Dropout Risk	Participation decline + feedback	Predict vendor disengagement
üü† Delayed Delivery Probability	Timeline variance trend	Forecast delay likelihood
‚úÖ Contract Success Likelihood	AI score + historical success	% chance of full delivery

‚öôÔ∏è Forecasting Flow (Backend/Client Logic):
Collect 6-month trailing data (from Supabase)

Normalize and weight factors using a formula

Output risk score (0‚Äì100 scale)

Flag: Low (<40), Medium (40‚Äì70), High (>70)

üß™ Example Risk Score Function:
js
Copy
Edit
const predictRiskScore = (metrics) => {
  const { slaBreaches, feedbackAvg, deliveryVariance, dropouts } = metrics;

  const score = (
    (slaBreaches * 0.3) +
    ((5 - feedbackAvg) * 0.3) +
    (deliveryVariance * 0.2) +
    (dropouts * 0.2)
  );

  return Math.min(100, Math.round(score));
};
üìà Visual Output:
üìä Risk Meter Chart (gauge)

üîÑ Trend Line (risk over time)

üîî Flags & Warnings in dashboard (e.g., ‚Äú‚ö†Ô∏è Vendor at risk of delay‚Äù)

from zipfile import ZipFile
from pathlib import Path

# Feedback Survey Form Component (React)
survey_form_jsx = """
// üìã Feedback Survey Form (React)
import React, { useState } from 'react';
import { supabase } from '../utils/supabaseClient';

const SurveyForm = ({ userId, vendorId, projectId }) => {
  const [form, setForm] = useState({
    satisfaction: 3,
    clarity: 3,
    communication: 3,
    delivery: 3,
    recommend: true,
    comments: ''
  });

  const handleSubmit = async () => {
    await supabase.from('feedback_submissions').insert([{ 
      user_id: userId,
      vendor_id: vendorId,
      project_id: projectId,
      ...form
    }]);
    alert("Thank you for your feedback!");
  };

  return (
    <div className="survey-form">
      {['satisfaction', 'clarity', 'communication', 'delivery'].map(field => (
        <div key={field}>
          <label>{field.charAt(0).toUpperCase() + field.slice(1)} (1-5):</label>
          <input type="number" min="1" max="5" value={form[field]} onChange={e => setForm({ ...form, [field]: parseInt(e.target.value) })} />
        </div>
      ))}
      <div>
        <label>Recommend vendor? </label>
        <input type="checkbox" checked={form.recommend} onChange={e => setForm({ ...form, recommend: e.target.checked })} />
      </div>
      <textarea placeholder="Any comments?" value={form.comments} onChange={e => setForm({ ...form, comments: e.target.value })} />
      <button onClick={handleSubmit}>Submit Feedback</button>
    </div>
  );
};

export default SurveyForm;
"""

# Survey Results Dashboard (basic)
survey_results_jsx = """
// üìä Survey Results Dashboard (React)
import React, { useEffect, useState } from 'react';
import { supabase } from '../utils/supabaseClient';
import { BarChart, Bar, XAxis, YAxis, Tooltip, ResponsiveContainer } from 'recharts';

const SurveyResultsDashboard = () => {
  const [data, setData] = useState([]);

  useEffect(() => {
    loadData();
  }, []);

  const loadData = async () => {
    const { data: responses } = await supabase.from('feedback_submissions').select('*');
    const metrics = ['satisfaction', 'clarity', 'communication', 'delivery'];
    const summary = metrics.map(key => ({
      metric: key,
      avg: (responses.reduce((acc, r) => acc + (r[key] || 0), 0) / responses.length).toFixed(2)
    }));
    setData(summary);
  };

  return (
    <ResponsiveContainer width="100%" height={300}>
      <BarChart data={data}>
        <XAxis dataKey="metric" />
        <YAxis domain={[0, 5]} />
        <Tooltip />
        <Bar dataKey="avg" fill="#3B82F6" />
      </BarChart>
    </ResponsiveContainer>
  );
};

export default SurveyResultsDashboard;
"""

# Risk Prediction Logic (JS)
risk_prediction_js = """
// üß† Predictive Risk Score Function
export const predictRiskScore = (metrics) => {
  const { slaBreaches, feedbackAvg, deliveryVariance, dropouts } = metrics;

  const score = (
    (slaBreaches * 0.3) +
    ((5 - feedbackAvg) * 0.3) +
    (deliveryVariance * 0.2) +
    (dropouts * 0.2)
  );

  return Math.min(100, Math.round(score));
};
"""

# Forecast Insights Panel (React)
forecast_panel_jsx = """
// üìà Forecast Insights Panel (React)
import React from 'react';
import { predictRiskScore } from './predictRiskScore';

const ForecastInsightsPanel = ({ metrics }) => {
  const riskScore = predictRiskScore(metrics);
  const riskLevel = riskScore > 70 ? 'HIGH' : riskScore > 40 ? 'MEDIUM' : 'LOW';
  const color = riskLevel === 'HIGH' ? 'red' : riskLevel === 'MEDIUM' ? 'orange' : 'green';

  return (
    <div className="forecast-panel">
      <h3>Contract Risk Score</h3>
      <div style={{ fontSize: '2rem', color }}>{riskScore}/100</div>
      <p>Risk Level: {riskLevel}</p>
    </div>
  );
};

export default ForecastInsightsPanel;
"""

# SQL for Feedback Table
sql_feedback_table = """
CREATE TABLE feedback_submissions (
  id UUID PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT gen_random_uuid(),
  user_id UUID REFERENCES users(id),
  vendor_id UUID REFERENCES vendors(id),
  project_id UUID,
  satisfaction INT,
  clarity INT,
  communication INT,
  delivery INT,
  recommend BOOLEAN,
  comments TEXT,
  created_at TIMESTAMP DEFAULT now()
);
"""

readme = """
# üìã Feedback Survey + Predictive Risk Module

## Included Components

- `SurveyForm.jsx`: Interactive feedback form with Supabase insert
- `SurveyResultsDashboard.jsx`: Chart-based visual of feedback trends
- `predictRiskScore.js`: Forecast risk score based on 4 KPIs
- `ForecastInsightsPanel.jsx`: Renders risk level + severity
- `feedback_submissions.sql`: Supabase schema for feedback

‚úÖ All components are React-ready. Insert into vendor or contract dashboard views.
"""

# Create ZIP package
zip_path = "/mnt/data/TendProcure_FeedbackRisk_Kit.zip"
file_structure = {
    "SurveyForm.jsx": survey_form_jsx,
    "SurveyResultsDashboard.jsx": survey_results_jsx,
    "predictRiskScore.js": risk_prediction_js,
    "ForecastInsightsPanel.jsx": forecast_panel_jsx,
    "feedback_submissions.sql": sql_feedback_table,
    "README.txt": readme
}

with ZipFile(zip_path, 'w') as zipf:
    for filename, content in file_structure.items():
        path = Path(f"/tmp/{filename}")
        path.write_text(content)
        zipf.write(path, arcname=filename)

zip_path

i am creating a web app for tender management and procurement excellence with so many modern enhance features for a  private company USA Industry based.
The idea is to source for tenderers to bid on project with respect to tender stages or steps to apply to take on the contract  for months of recurring property management services such as electrical maintenance, house keeping , HVac install and maintenance, painting and so many more.  once new tenderers reach out to apply to take on this contract bids for each of the tender project on the site . they will have to open the notice inviting tender page , then commence action for each steps as further detailed below.

Tender Process Workflow for New Tenderers

Notice Inviting Tender (NIT)
The project is announced, detailing the scope of supplies, services, or construction works.
Tenders are alerted and encouraged to respond appropriately based on detailed information provided.
Pre-Qualification (PQ)
Contractors submit applications demonstrating qualification and suitability, often through technical bids.
The purpose is to identify eligible and capable contractors to proceed to the next stage.
Issue of Tender Documents
Qualified contractors purchase or download tender documents from the website.
The documents contain detailed contract clauses, terms, and conditions needed for bidding.
Site Investigation
Contractors observe and assess the site conditions, terrain, source of materials, and nearby vendors.
This helps in understanding project specifics and planning accordingly.
Tender Summary
Contractors review a summary of the main contractual clauses, including interest rates, advance clauses, and other critical conditions.
Analysis of Costs
Contractors analyze project costs, including:
Direct Costs (DC): Labour, materials, machinery.
Indirect Costs (IDC): Overheads, insurance, travel, schedule delays (estimated at 5% of contract value).
Profit Margin: Typically 10-15%.
Contract Value (CV): Sum of direct costs, indirect costs, profit margin, risk, and opportunities.
Bid Submission
Contractors prepare and submit:
Technical bids (pre-qualified earlier),
Financial bids,
Earnest Money Deposit (EMD) of 2% of estimated cost (serves as bid security).
EMD submission is mandatory; without it, the bid is invalid.
Bid Evaluation
The organization reviews submissions, checking for abnormally low/high bids.
Evaluation involves technical and financial scoring to identify the best bid.
Letter of Acceptance (LOA)
The lowest qualified bidder (L1) is issued an LOA after successful bid evaluation.
Submission of Required Documents by L1 Contractor
Accepted contractor submits:
Performance Bank Guarantee (PBG) of 3% of the quoted value (refundable after project completion).
Valid Labour Licenses.
Signing of Contract Agreement
The contractor and organization sign formal contracts, initiating legal obligations.
Project Advances
Organization provides mobilization and material advances to the contractor to facilitate project startup.
Project Commencement
Contractors start work onsite, utilizing advances for mobilization, procurement, and preparation.
Execution and Monitoring
Execution of project tasks, site planning, procurement, and operations occur.
Invoices are submitted for expenses.
A 50% security deposit is refunded after the defect liability period, assuming no issues.
Terms of Payment
The agreed payment schedule includes considerations such as defect liability period, retention money, EOT, bonuses, escalation, and payment methods to subcontractors.
Claims and Dispute Resolution
Handling scope changes, delays, claims, and disputes through negotiations, arbitration, litigation, or conciliation.
Completion Phase
Handover
The contractor officially hands over the completed project.
Final responsibilities and accomplishments are summarized.
DLP (Defect Liability Period)
Contractor addresses any defects found during the liability period.
Refunds of PBG, security deposits, and bonus payments are processed.
Final Completion Certificate
Submission of final documentation confirming project completion under quality and safety standards.
The project is formally closed and handed over.
Major Tender Sources for Real Estate & Property Management
Construction & Renovation Vendors (builders, contractors)
Material & Fixture Suppliers (furnishings, finishing materials)
Maintenance & Handyman Services (plumbing, electrical, repairs)
Cleaning & Waste Management (janitorial, waste disposal)
Security & Facility Management (security personnel, HVAC, landscaping)
Professional Services (architects, legal, real estate brokers)
Technology & Software Providers (management systems, security tech)
Insurance & Financial Services (property insurance, valuation)
Logistics & Moving Vendors (movers, storage)
Specialized Contractors (elevators, energy systems, landscaping)

Intuitive Dashboard Design:


Create a visually appealing and customizable dashboard that provides users with a quick overview of key metrics, active tenders, performance analytics, and other relevant data.
Implement role-based dashboards to cater to the specific needs of property managers, contractors, vendors, finance teams, and administrators.
Incorporate interactive widgets, data visualization tools, and customizable reporting capabilities to empower users to make data-driven decisions.


Streamlined Tender Management:


Develop a central tender management module that offers a unified view of all tenders, with advanced filtering, search, and sorting capabilities.
Integrate a kanban board or calendar view to provide users with a clear visual representation of the tender lifecycle and associated milestones.
Implement a user-friendly tender creation process, with pre-built templates, AI-powered suggestions, and a comprehensive requirements builder to simplify the process.
Ensure seamless integration between the tender details page, document management, bid submissions, evaluation, and contract management workflows.


Intelligent Bid Management:


Create a dedicated bid management module that allows contractors and vendors to easily submit, track, and manage their bids.
Incorporate a smart bid submission interface with features like auto-save, version control, team collaboration, and a pre-submission checklist to enhance the user experience.
Leverage AI-powered tools to assist contractors in generating competitive bids, analyzing market trends, and evaluating their win probability.
Provide a comprehensive bid library, enabling users to access and learn from previous successful submissions.


Efficient Evaluation and Awards:


Develop a robust evaluation module that supports collaborative review, scoring, and decision-making processes.
Implement customizable approval workflows and escalation rules to ensure a transparent and streamlined evaluation process.
Integrate AI-powered tools to assist the evaluation panel in automated scoring, bias detection, risk assessment, and compliance verification.
Automate the award management process, including the generation of award letters, contract creation, and seamless notification to all stakeholders.


Comprehensive Contract Management:


Offer a centralized contract management interface that allows users to easily access, review, and monitor contract details, terms, and performance metrics.
Implement features for contract creation, digital signatures, payment schedules, milestone tracking, and change order management.
Incorporate advanced performance management capabilities, including KPI dashboards, service-level tracking, and issue resolution workflows.
Leverage predictive analytics and market intelligence to support data-driven decision-making during contract renewals and negotiations.


Vendor and Contractor Hub:


Develop a vendor and contractor directory that provides detailed profiles, capabilities, certifications, and performance ratings.

Tender Creation & Submission Errors
Diagnosis & Fix Template
Diagnosis Steps:
Check form validation errors (client-side & server-side).
Verify data submitted aligns with schema constraints.
Review logs for validation failures or server errors.
Confirm API endpoints are correctly called and respond properly.
Test submitting with minimal data to isolate issues.
Cross-check user permissions for submission rights.
Possible Causes:

Missing or invalid required fields.
API endpoint misconfiguration.
Permission issues.
Server-side validation logic errors.
Script or frontend bugs.
Fix Strategy:

Correct form validation rules.
Fix API endpoint URLs or request payloads.
Update user roles/permissions.
Adjust server validation logic.
Debug frontend JavaScript to ensure proper data submission.
Verification:

Test submitting valid and invalid data.
Confirm logs show successful API calls.
Check database updates and audit logs.
Conduct end-to-end testing.
2. Bid Submission & Evaluation Failures
Diagnosis & Fix
Diagnosis:

Review bid upload logs, file format, and size.
Check for errors in file storage or access rights.
Validate API or backend processing of bids.
Confirm bidder roles and permissions.
Test with different file formats and sizes.
Fix:

Enforce file size & format constraints.
Fix file path or storage permission issues.
Adjust upload handling code for robustness.
Ensure secure, HTTPS access.
Implement fallback or retry mechanisms.
Verification:

Upload test bids.
Validate successful storage and retrieval.
Confirm evaluation process triggers correctly.
Check for clean audit trail.
3. Approval & Authorization Conflicts
Diagnosis & Fix
Diagnosis:

Check user roles and permissions configuration.
Review access control logic.
Review audit logs for blocked actions.
Confirm API permissions are correct.
Fix:

Adjust role permissions to match workflows.
Correct authorization middleware.
Update access control rules.
Notify users if permissions have changed.
Verification:

Re-test user actions.
Verify auditing logs.
Ensure only authorized users can perform sensitive operations.
4. Contract Generation & Management Bugs
Diagnosis & Fix
Diagnosis:

Review contract generation code.
Check dynamic data input/output.
Test specific scenarios (e.g., different tender types).
Fix:

Correct data bindings.
Handle edge cases (missing data).
Fix formatting or field mismatch issues.
Add error handling for failures.
Verification:

Generate contracts with varied data.
Confirm contract accuracy.
Ensure the PDF or output format is correct.
Validate digital signatures/security if applicable.
5. Notifications & Email Delivery Failures
Diagnosis & Fix
Diagnosis:

Check SMTP/email service logs.
Validate email template syntax.
Confirm email addresses are valid.
Test email sending with various templates.
Fix:

Correct email address validation.
Update email templates to avoid syntax issues.
Fix SMTP configuration issues.
Add retries or fallback options.
Verification:

Send test emails.
Check email logs and delivery reports.
Confirm recipients receive emails promptly and correctly.
6. Authentication & Role-Based Access Control (RBAC) Issues
Diagnosis & Fix
Diagnosis:

Review user roles and permissions.
Inspect authentication middleware.
Test various user roles accessing modules.
Fix:

Update role permission mappings.
Fix logic in middleware for role checks.
Ensure proper token/credential validation.
Re-assign or create roles as needed.
Verification:

Login as different roles.
Confirm access rights are enforced properly.
Check security logs for anomalies.
7. External API & Integration Failures
Diagnosis & Fix
Diagnosis:

Check API response statuses.
Inspect request/response payloads.
Confirm API keys, tokens, endpoints.
Test with Postman or curl.
Fix:

Correct API URL, headers, or payload.
Refresh API keys if expired.
Handle errors gracefully.
Add retries where appropriate.
Verification:

Re-test integration points.
Confirm data flow and responses.
Log API interactions for future audits.
8. Performance Bottlenecks & Scalability Issues
Diagnosis & Fix
Diagnosis:

Use profiling tools (e.g., Chrome DevTools, server profilers).
Monitor database query performance.
Review API response times.
Check server load and resource utilization.
Fix:

Optimize slow queries.
Add caching layers.
Refactor bottleneck code.
Scale horizontally or vertically if needed.
Verification:

Run load tests.
Measure before-and-after performance.
Ensure system remains stable under load.
9. Security & Data Privacy Flaws
Diagnosis & Fix
Diagnosis:

Conduct security scans.
Review permission and access control logic.
Check for data breaches or leaks.
Validate data encryption and secure storage.
Fix:

Harden access controls.
Encrypt sensitive data.
Patch known vulnerabilities.
Implement secure coding practices.
Verification:

Run security audits.
Conduct penetration testing.
Review logs for suspicious activity.
10. Deployment & Environment Configuration Issues
Diagnosis & Fix
Diagnosis:

Check environment variables and config files.
Verify deployment scripts.
Review server logs.
Confirm consistent environment setups across dev/staging/production.
Fix:

Correct environment variables.
Fix deployment scripts or CI/CD pipelines.
Sync configuration files.
Automate environment validation checks.
Verification:

Redeploy in staging.
Perform smoke tests.
Confirm configuration correctness.
Final Note: All-in-One Strategy for Success
Ultimate Operating Principles for Your Team/Assistants:

Always analyze deeply; root cause analysis first.
Use verified tools and methods‚Äînever guess.
Persist until the issue is 100% resolved*.
Use minimal, scalable fixes‚Äîavoid overcomplication.
Document all findings, decisions, tests, and fixes.
Think strategically: prevent future issues, ensure security, AND optimize performance.
Prioritize quality over quick fixes‚Äîaim for robustness and maintainability.

You said:
Also take note my idea plan earlier which you can still modify and enhance you dont need to stick to my plan only , But i just want you to know this down 

Tender Process Workflow for New Tenderers
1. Notice Inviting Tender (NIT)
The project is announced, detailing the scope of supplies, services, or construction works.
Tenders are alerted and encouraged to respond appropriately based on detailed information provided.
2. Pre-Qualification (PQ)
Contractors submit applications demonstrating qualification and suitability, often through technical bids.
The purpose is to identify eligible and capable contractors to proceed to the next stage.
3. Issue of Tender Documents
Qualified contractors purchase or download tender documents from the website.
The documents contain detailed contract clauses, terms, and conditions needed for bidding.
4. Site Investigation
Contractors observe and assess the site conditions, terrain, source of materials, and nearby vendors.
This helps in understanding project specifics and planning accordingly.
5. Tender Summary
Contractors review a summary of the main contractual clauses, including interest rates, advance clauses, and other critical conditions.
6. Analysis of Costs
Contractors analyze project costs, including:
Direct Costs (DC): Labour, materials, machinery.
Indirect Costs (IDC): Overheads, insurance, travel, schedule delays (estimated at 5% of contract value).
Profit Margin: Typically 10-15%.
Contract Value (CV): Sum of direct costs, indirect costs, profit margin, risk, and opportunities.
7. Bid Submission
Contractors prepare and submit:
Technical bids (pre-qualified earlier),
Financial bids,
Earnest Money Deposit (EMD) of 2% of estimated cost (serves as bid security).
EMD submission is mandatory; without it, the bid is invalid.
8. Bid Evaluation
The organization reviews submissions, checking for abnormally low/high bids.
Evaluation involves technical and financial scoring to identify the best bid.
9. Letter of Acceptance (LOA)
The lowest qualified bidder (L1) is issued an LOA after successful bid evaluation.
10. Submission of Required Documents by L1 Contractor
Accepted contractor submits:
Performance Bank Guarantee (PBG) of 3% of the quoted value (refundable after project completion).
Valid Labour Licenses.
11. Signing of Contract Agreement
The contractor and organization sign formal contracts, initiating legal obligations.
12. Project Advances
Organization provides mobilization and material advances to the contractor to facilitate project startup.
13. Project Commencement
Contractors start work onsite, utilizing advances for mobilization, procurement, and preparation.
14. Execution and Monitoring
Execution of project tasks, site planning, procurement, and operations occur.
Invoices are submitted for expenses.
A 50% security deposit is refunded after the defect liability period, assuming no issues.
15. Terms of Payment
The agreed payment schedule includes considerations such as defect liability period, retention money, EOT, bonuses, escalation, and payment methods to subcontractors.
16. Claims and Dispute Resolution
Handling scope changes, delays, claims, and disputes through negotiations, arbitration, litigation, or conciliation.
Completion Phase
17. Handover
The contractor officially hands over the completed project.
Final responsibilities and accomplishments are summarized.
18. DLP (Defect Liability Period)
Contractor addresses any defects found during the liability period.
Refunds of PBG, security deposits, and bonus payments are processed.
19. Final Completion Certificate
Submission of final documentation confirming project completion under quality and safety standards.
The project is formally closed and handed over.

Then Proceed with any next actions you suggest

üîê Supabase Table Structure (notifications)
Field	Type	Description
id	uuid	Primary key
user_id	uuid	Recipient user
title	text	Notification title
body	text	Description / body
type	text	'info', 'warning', 'alert', etc.
read	boolean	Whether the user read it
created_at	timestamp	Auto-generated

üì¨ notificationService.js
js
Copy
Edit
import { supabase } from './client'

export async function fetchNotifications(userId) {
  let { data, error } = await supabase
    .from('notifications')
    .select('*')
    .eq('user_id', userId)
    .order('created_at', { ascending: false })
  return { data, error }
}

export async function markAsRead(notificationId) {
  return await supabase
    .from('notifications')
    .update({ read: true })
    .eq('id', notificationId)
}

function generatePDF() {

const data = {
  contractTitle: "HVAC Upgrade Agreement",
  vendorName: "AirPros Inc.",
  startDate: "2025-07-10",
  scopeDetails: "Maintain and upgrade systems in 6 facilities.",
  milestones: ["Kickoff", "30% Progress", "Final Delivery"]
};

for (let key in data) {
  if (key === 'milestones') {
    const list = document.getElementById('milestonesList');
    data[key].forEach(m => {
      const li = document.createElement("li");
      li.innerText = m;
      list.appendChild(li);
    });
  } else {
    document.getElementById(key).innerText = data[key];
  }
}

üßæ Sample Tender Input:
json
Copy
Edit
{
  "title": "HVAC Maintenance - Miami Zone",
  "services_required": ["HVAC", "Inspection"],
  "min_capacity": 10,
  "region": "Florida",
  "required_certs": ["OSHA"]
}
‚öôÔ∏è Basic JS Matching Logic:
js
Copy
Edit
function matchVendors(tender, vendors) {
  return vendors.map(vendor => {
    let score = 0;

    if (vendor.region === tender.region) score += 2;
    if (vendor.capacity >= tender.min_capacity) score += 2;

    const matchingServices = tender.services_required.filter(service =>
      vendor.services.includes(service)
    );
    score += matchingServices.length * 1.5;

    const matchingCerts = tender.required_certs.filter(cert =>
      vendor.certifications.includes(cert)
    );
    score += matchingCerts.length * 1.5;

    return { ...vendor, score };
  }).sort((a, b) => b.score - a.score);
}
Use matchVendors(tender, vendorList) to return best-fit vendors.

‚úÖ 1. Supabase Edge Function ‚Äì AI Onboarding Flow (Vendors)
Goal: Automate AI onboarding based on the 19-step tenderer workflow.

Tasks:

Scaffold Supabase Edge Function:

Triggered on new vendor registration.

Calls OpenAI function calling or internal logic to walk through onboarding stages.

Updates user profile with onboarding progress.

File: onboarding.ts

ts
Copy
Edit
import { serve } from 'https://deno.land/std@0.168.0/http/server.ts'
import { createClient } from 'https://esm.sh/@supabase/supabase-js'

serve(async (req) => {
  const supabase = createClient(
    Deno.env.get('SUPABASE_URL')!,
    Deno.env.get('SUPABASE_SERVICE_ROLE_KEY')!
  )

  const { user_id } = await req.json()

  // Simulated onboarding stages for vendor
  const onboardingSteps = [
    "Notice Inviting Tender",
    "Pre-Qualification",
    "Tender Document Issue",
    "Site Investigation",
    "Cost Analysis",
    "Bid Submission",
    "Bid Evaluation",
    "Letter of Acceptance",
    "Contract Signing",
    "Project Execution"
  ]

  await supabase
    .from('vendor_onboarding')
    .insert(onboardingSteps.map((step, index) => ({
      user_id,
      step,
      status: index === 0 ? 'active' : 'pending'
    })))

  return new Response(JSON.stringify({ message: "Onboarding initiated." }), {
    headers: { "Content-Type": "application/json" }
  })
})

‚úÖ 3. Notifications System (Frontend + Supabase)
Frontend Component Example (React):

tsx
Copy
Edit
// NotificationBell.tsx
import { useEffect, useState } from 'react'
import { supabase } from '../lib/supabaseClient'

export function NotificationBell() {
  const [notifications, setNotifications] = useState([])

  useEffect(() => {
    const fetchNotifications = async () => {
      const { data, error } = await supabase
        .from('notifications')
        .select('*')
        .order('created_at', { ascending: false })
      setNotifications(data)
    }

    fetchNotifications()

    const subscription = supabase
      .channel('notifications')
      .on('postgres_changes', { event: '*', schema: 'public', table: 'notifications' },
        payload => {
          setNotifications((prev) => [payload.new, ...prev])
        }
      ).subscribe()

    return () => {
      subscription.unsubscribe()
    }
  }, [])

  return (
    <div className="relative">
      <button>üîî {notifications.length}</button>
      <div className="absolute z-10 bg-white border shadow p-2">
        {notifications.map(n => (
          <div key={n.id} className="text-sm">{n.message}</div>
        ))}
      </div>
    </div>
  )
}
üì° Backend: Supabase trigger + function to insert notification on new tender status, contract stage update, etc.

‚úÖ 4. PDF Contract Generator (HTML + JS)
Initial structure using jsPDF:

html
Copy
Edit
<!-- HTML Template -->
<div id="contract-template">
  <h1>Contract Agreement</h1>
  <p>Client: <span id="client-name">TendCorp Inc.</span></p>
  <p>Vendor: <span id="vendor-name">ABC Services</span></p>
  <p>Start Date: <span id="start-date">2025-07-15</span></p>
  <!-- more fields... -->
</div>

<!-- JS PDF Export -->
<script>
import jsPDF from 'jspdf'
import html2canvas from 'html2canvas'

function generatePDF() {
  const doc = new jsPDF()
  html2canvas(document.getElementById('contract-template')).then(canvas => {
    const imgData = canvas.toDataURL('image/png')
    doc.addImage(imgData, 'PNG', 10, 10)
    doc.save('Contract_Agreement.pdf')
  })
}
</script>

‚úÖ SQL Table Scaffolding (Supabase)
sql
Copy
Edit
-- Vendors Table
CREATE TABLE vendors (
  id UUID PRIMARY KEY,
  company_name TEXT,
  contact_email TEXT,
  certified BOOLEAN,
  rating FLOAT,
  registration_date TIMESTAMP DEFAULT now()
);

-- Tenders Table
CREATE TABLE tenders (
  id UUID PRIMARY KEY,
  title TEXT,
  description TEXT,
  status TEXT,
  created_at TIMESTAMP DEFAULT now()
);

-- Bids Table
CREATE TABLE bids (
  id UUID PRIMARY KEY,
  vendor_id UUID REFERENCES vendors(id),
  tender_id UUID REFERENCES tenders(id),
  amount NUMERIC,
  submitted_at TIMESTAMP
);

-- Contracts Table
CREATE TABLE contracts (
  id UUID PRIMARY KEY,
  tender_id UUID,
  vendor_id UUID,
  start_date DATE,
  end_date DATE,
  status TEXT
);

-- Notifications Table
CREATE TABLE notifications (
  id UUID PRIMARY KEY,
  user_id UUID,
  title TEXT,
  message TEXT,
  seen BOOLEAN DEFAULT FALSE,
  created_at TIMESTAMP DEFAULT now()
);

-- Escrow Transactions
CREATE TABLE escrow_payments (
  id UUID PRIMARY KEY,
  contract_id UUID,
  amount NUMERIC,
  status TEXT,
  released_at TIMESTAMP
);

ts
Copy
Edit
// Send notification on new tender
create or replace function notify_new_tender()
returns trigger as $$
begin
  insert into notifications(user_id, title, message)
  values (NEW.user_id, 'New Tender Available', 'A new tender has been posted. Check it out!');
  return NEW;
end;
$$ language plpgsql;
Frontend React Hook

tsx
Copy
Edit
const fetchNotifications = async (userId) => {
  const { data, error } = await supabase
    .from('notifications')
    .select('*')
    .eq('user_id', userId)
    .order('created_at', { ascending: false });

  return data;
};

‚úÖ üìç Escrow Payment Flow
1. SQL Table Setup: escrow_payments
sql
Copy
Edit
CREATE TABLE escrow_payments (
  id UUID PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT gen_random_uuid(),
  contract_id UUID REFERENCES contracts(id),
  amount NUMERIC,
  status TEXT DEFAULT 'pending', -- pending | released | blocked
  milestone TEXT,
  released_at TIMESTAMP,
  created_at TIMESTAMP DEFAULT now()
);
2. Logic for Release After Milestone (Edge Function Sketch)
ts
Copy
Edit
export const handleEscrowRelease = async ({ contractId, milestone }) => {
  const { data, error } = await supabase
    .from("contracts")
    .select("milestone_status")
    .eq("id", contractId)
    .single();

  if (data.milestone_status.includes(milestone)) {
    await supabase
      .from("escrow_payments")
      .update({ status: "released", released_at: new Date() })
      .match({ contract_id: contractId, milestone });
  }
};
3. Frontend (Finance Role) Form (React)
jsx
Copy
Edit

  <Input name="contractId" placeholder="Contract ID" />

    <option value="mobilization">Mobilization</option>
    <option value="halfway">50% Milestone</option>
    <option value="completion">Completion</option>
  </Select>
  <Button onClick={handleEscrowRelease}>Release Funds</Button>
</Form>

‚úÖ üõ† Property AI Auto-Repair System
SQL: repair_requests
sql
Copy
Edit
CREATE TABLE repair_requests (
  id UUID PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT gen_random_uuid(),
  property_id UUID REFERENCES properties(id),
  request_type TEXT,
  status TEXT DEFAULT 'open',
  assigned_vendor UUID REFERENCES vendors(id),
  created_at TIMESTAMP DEFAULT now()
);
Auto-Routing Logic:
ts
Copy
Edit
const routeRepairRequest = async (propertyId, requestType) => {
  const { data: vendors } = await supabase
    .from("vendors")
    .select("*")
    .ilike("services", `%${requestType}%`);

  const nearest = vendors[0]; // Add distance logic later
  await supabase
    .from("repair_requests")
    .insert({ property_id: propertyId, request_type, assigned_vendor: nearest.id });
};

with ZipFile(zip_path, "w") as zipf:
    for name, content in html_templates.items():
        html_file = f"/mnt/data/{name}"
        with open(html_file, "w") as f:
            f.write(content)
        zipf.write(html_file, arcname=name)

    for name, content in sql_scripts.items():

‚úÖ TendProcure Admin Master Guide
üë§ User Roles & Setup
Roles:

Admin ‚Äì Full control over system settings, users, approvals.

Vendor ‚Äì Can view/apply to tenders, submit bids, manage contracts.

Contractor ‚Äì Handles site execution, documentation, and milestones.

PM (Project Manager) ‚Äì Oversees execution, progress, QA/QC.

Finance ‚Äì Manages payments, escrow release, vendor payouts.

Admin Tasks:

Invite new users ‚Üí Assign roles ‚Üí Monitor activity.

Deactivate/re-assign accounts securely via RBAC policy.

üìã Tender Creation Checklist
Required Fields:

Scope of work, deadline, budget, location, attached docs.

Validation Steps:

Auto-checks for incomplete fields or invalid file formats.

Workflow:

Draft ‚Üí Review (PM/Finance) ‚Üí Final Approval ‚Üí Publish.

üìÑ Contract Generation
Use the PDF template editor to bind dynamic values.

Trigger from awarded Tender:

Assign ‚Üí Prefill ‚Üí Review ‚Üí Generate PDF.

E-Signature:

Integrated via Supabase functions or third-party API (e.g., SignWell).

üí∏ Escrow Release Guide
Milestone Creation:

Admin/PM defines deliverables (e.g., Foundation Complete).

Triggering Payout:

PM approves ‚Üí Finance releases ‚Üí Logs updated.

Logs:

Supabase logs + contract escrow history shown per vendor.

üîî Notifications & Alerts
Supabase triggers listen for:

Tender publication

Bid submission success

Contract signature

Escrow release

Channels:

Push, email, or dashboard bell alerts.

Templates:

Stored in Supabase DB as markdown/HTML blocks.

üßæ Bid and Evaluation Overview
Scoring Workflow:

Technical (weight 60%) + Financial (40%)

AI Scoring Assistant:

NLP parses technical docs, checks compliance, ranks risk.

Manual Review Layer:

PM & Admin make final decisions before award.

üõ† Repair Management Flow
Auto-create request via:

Vendor report / PM log / Resident AI monitor

Assign to qualified vendors by:

Matching tags (e.g., Plumbing, HVAC)

Status:

Pending ‚Üí In Progress ‚Üí Resolved ‚Üí Closed

üß† AI Modules Explained
Fraud Scoring:

Vector similarity + anomaly detection (past vendor history)

Dispute Resolution:

Prompt-based AI mediator recommends next steps.

Recommendation Engine:

NLP parses vendor profile ‚Üí compares tags + bids ‚Üí scores match.

üõ°Ô∏è Security & Compliance
RBAC powered by Supabase policies

GDPR checklist enabled (opt-in terms, data access logs)

Regular backups via Supabase Storage backup system

üìñ FAQ (for user section)
Why can‚Äôt I submit a tender?
You must have an Admin or PM role. Check permissions.

Why are vendors unverified?
Ensure they complete all KYC + document uploads.

How is bid scoring calculated?
Based on weighted metrics, technical doc relevance, cost efficiency.

What happens when a contract is overdue?
PM flags it ‚Üí Admin escalates ‚Üí Dispute module can be triggered.

# üèóÔ∏è TendProcure - Tender & Procurement Management Web App

TendProcure is a fullstack tendering platform for managing vendor procurement, bids, contracts, analytics, AI recommendations, and property service workflows.

---

## üöÄ Tech Stack

- **Frontend**: React + TailwindCSS + Vercel Hosting  
- **Backend**: Supabase (PostgreSQL, Auth, Edge Functions)  
- **AI**: GPT-4o / Embeddings (Vendor Matching, Fraud Scoring)  
- **Hosting**: Vercel + GitHub + Supabase  
- **Dev Env**: GitHub Codespaces + Devcontainers

---

# üí∞ Payment Escrow Process

TendProcure holds project payments in escrow until key milestones are verified. Process:

1. Milestone submitted by vendor
2. PM verifies delivery
3. Finance approves release
4. Vendor paid via connected wallet

# TendProcure - Tender & Procurement Platform

## Getting Started via Codespaces

1. Create Codespace on this repo  
2. Run:
   ```bash
   npm install
   npx supabase start
   npm run dev
Develop in VSCode, preview frontend at localhost:3000, Supabase at localhost:54321.

Folder Overview
src/‚Ää‚Äî‚ÄäUI components, pages, services

supabase/‚Ää‚Äî‚ÄäSQL migrations, Supabase Edge functions

sql/‚Ää‚Äî‚ÄäStandalone SQL table definitions

docs/‚Ää‚Äî‚ÄäOperational manuals & guides

Modules
Vendor onboarding

Notification & Escrow flows

AI-powered fraud detection & dispute resolution

Property repair auto-requests

‚úÖ 3. SQL Table Scaffolds
sql/vendors_table.sql
sql
Copy
Edit
CREATE TABLE vendors (
  id UUID PRIMARY KEY,
  company_name TEXT,
  contact_email TEXT,
  certified BOOLEAN,
  rating FLOAT,
  registration_date TIMESTAMP DEFAULT now()
);
(The other SQL files are similar, as defined previously.)

‚öôÔ∏è 4. Supabase Edge Function Starters
supabase/functions/onboarding.js
js
Copy
Edit
import { createClient } from '@supabase/supabase-js'

export const handler = async (req, res) => {
  const supabase = createClient(process.env.SUPABASE_URL, process.env.SUPABASE_SERVICE_ROLE_KEY);
  const { user_id } = req.body;
  const steps = [/* 19-step flow */];
  const payload = steps.map((s, i) => ({user_id, step: s, status: i === 0 ? 'active' : 'pending'}));
  await supabase.from('vendor_onboarding').insert(payload);
  res.json({ message: 'Onboarding initiated'});
}
notify_new_tender.js and escrow_release.js can follow similar patterns when triggered by Supabase DB hooks.

‚úÖ 5. Docs Folder (Samples)

docs/OnboardingGuide.md ‚Äî step-by-step vendor onboarding flows.

docs/EscrowFlow.md ‚Äî guide for payment escrow release logic.

Create the folder structure and files
for folder, files in structure.items():
folder_path = os.path.join(base_path, folder)
os.makedirs(folder_path, exist_ok=True)
for filename, content in files.items():
with open(os.path.join(folder_path, filename), "w") as f:
f.write(content.strip())

Create a ZIP file
zip_path = f"{base_path}.zip"
with ZipFile(zip_path, 'w') as zipf:
for root, dirs, files in os.walk(base_path):
for file in files:
file_path = os.path.join(root, file)
zipf.write(file_path, arcname=os.path.relpath(file_path, base_path))

## 1. Vision and Platform Goals

- Build **TendProcure**, a cutting-edge B2B tender lifecycle platform.
- Modular architecture with role-based dashboards.
- Integrate AI (vendor scoring, onboarding, fraud detection, NLP matching).
- Streamline contract creation, dispute resolution, and escrow flows.
- Enable mobile-first experience with smart tutorials and guides.

---

## 2. Modules & Features

- [x] üß≠ Tender Lifecycle Tracker
- [x] ü§ñ Vendor Recommendation Engine (Embedding + Vector Search)
- [x] üìë Auto PDF Contract Generator
- [x] üîî Notification System (Supabase Realtime + Custom Alerts)
- [x] üìä Tender Analytics Dashboard
- [x] üì¶ Document Management + Digital Signature Integration
- [x] ü§ù Vendor Onboarding Flow (AI Assistant-powered)
- [x] üîê RBAC + Secure Auth Flow
- [ ] üí∏ Payment Escrow Module
- [ ] ‚öñ Dispute Resolution AI Engine
- [ ] üö® Tender Fraud Scoring System
- [ ] üèöÔ∏è AI Auto-Repair Requests

---

## 3. Technical Architecture

- **Frontend**: React (Next.js), TailwindCSS, Vercel
- **Backend**: Supabase (PostgreSQL + pgvector + Edge Functions)
- **AI Stack**: GPT-4o, Embeddings, Supabase Functions
- **DevOps**: GitHub Codespaces, CI/CD, `.devcontainer.json`

- üìå Tender Lifecycle Overview

## 5. AI Assistant Strategy

- Role-aware AI flows per user type
- Vendor onboarding AI: walks through 19-step tenderer process
- NLP Matching: Semantic search + embedding comparisons
- Fraud detection AI: Risk scoring + anomaly flagging
